I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Testing of rune effects is broken
### Describe the bug

Testing rune effects as described in [Svelte documentation](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/testing#Unit-and-integration-testing-using-Vitest-Using-runes-inside-your-test-files) is broken in Svelte > 5.1.11 and is double broken with vitest 3.2.x

Repo has `logger.svelte.test.js` from documentation with latest svelte and vitest versions. Its expectation fails as `flushSync()` seems to be ignored and code in $effect rune is not run.

Downgrading vitest version to 3.1.4 changes test behavior - it fails with `effect_update_depth_exceeded`.

Downgrading Svelte as well to 5.1.11 or older makes test to pass.

### Reproduction

Repo: https://github.com/vits/vitest-svelte-effects

    46	/**
    47	 * Returns an [`AbortSignal`](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/AbortSignal) that aborts when the current [derived](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/$derived) or [effect](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/$effect) re-runs or is destroyed.
    48	 *
    49	 * Must be called while a derived or effect is running.
    50	 *
    51	 * ```svelte
    52	 * <script>
    53	 *      import { getAbortSignal } from 'svelte';
    54	 *
    55	 *      let { id } = $props();
    56	 *
    57	 *      async function getData(id) {
    58	 *              const response = await fetch(`/items/${id}`, {
    59	 *                      signal: getAbortSignal()
    60	 *              });
    61	 *
    62	 *              return await response.json();
    63	 *      }
    64	 *
    65	 *      const data = $derived(await getData(id));
    66	 * </script>
    67	 * ```
    68	 */
    69	export function getAbortSignal() {
    70	        if (active_reaction === null) {
    71	                e.get_abort_signal_outside_reaction();
    72	        }
    73	
    74	        return (active_reaction.ac ??= new AbortController()).signal;

    77	/**
    78	 * `onMount`, like [`$effect`](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/$effect), schedules a function to run as soon as the component has been mounted to the DOM.
    79	 * Unlike `$effect`, the provided function only runs once.
    80	 *
    81	 * It must be called during the component's initialisation (but doesn't need to live _inside_ the component;
    82	 * it can be called from an external module). If a function is returned _synchronously_ from `onMount`,
    83	 * it will be called when the component is unmounted.
    84	 *
    85	 * `onMount` functions do not run during [server-side rendering](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/svelte-server#render).
    86	 *
    87	 * @template T
    88	 * @param {() => NotFunction<T> | Promise<NotFunction<T>> | (() => any)} fn
    89	 * @returns {void}
    90	 */
    91	export function onMount(fn) {
    92	        if (component_context === null) {
    93	                e.lifecycle_outside_component('onMount');
    94	        }
    95	
    96	        if (legacy_mode_flag && component_context.l !== null) {
    97	                init_update_callbacks(component_context).m.push(fn);
    98	        } else {
    99	                user_effect(() => {
   100	                        const cleanup = untrack(fn);
   101	                        if (typeof cleanup === 'function') return /** @type {() => void} */ (cleanup);
   102	                });
   103	        }
   104	}
   105	
   106	/**
   107	 * Schedules a callback to run immediately before the component is unmounted.
   108	 *
   109	 * Out of `onMount`, `beforeUpdate`, `afterUpdate` and `onDestroy`, this is the
   110	 * only one that runs inside a server-side component.
   111	 *
   112	 * @param {() => any} fn
   113	 * @returns {void}
   114	 */
   115	export function onDestroy(fn) {
   116	        if (component_context === null) {
   117	                e.lifecycle_outside_component('onDestroy');
   118	        }
   119	
   120	        onMount(() => () => untrack(fn));
   121	}
   122	
   123	/**
   124	 * @template [T=any]
   125	 * @param {string} type
   126	 * @param {T} [detail]
   127	 * @param {any}params_0
   128	 * @returns {CustomEvent<T>}
   129	 */
   130	function create_custom_event(type, detail, { bubbles = false, cancelable = false } = {}) {
   131	        return new CustomEvent(type, { detail, bubbles, cancelable });
   132	}
   133	
   134	/**
   135	 * Creates an event dispatcher that can be used to dispatch [component events](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/legacy-on#Component-events).
   136	 * Event dispatchers are functions that can take two arguments: `name` and `detail`.
   137	 *
   138	 * Component events created with `createEventDispatcher` create a
   139	 * [CustomEvent](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/CustomEvent).
   140	 * These events do not [bubble](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Learn/JavaScript/Building_blocks/Events#Event_bubbling_and_capture).
   141	 * The `detail` argument corresponds to the [CustomEvent.detail](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/CustomEvent/detail)
   142	 * property and can contain any type of data.
   143	 *
   144	 * The event dispatcher can be typed to narrow the allowed event names and the type of the `detail` argument:
   145	 * ```ts
   146	 * const dispatch = createEventDispatcher<{
   147	 *  loaded: null; // does not take a detail argument
   148	 *  change: string; // takes a detail argument of type string, which is required
   149	 *  optional: number | null; // takes an optional detail argument of type number
   150	 * }>();
   151	 * ```
   152	 *
   153	 * @deprecated Use callback props and/or the `$host()` rune instead — see [migration guide](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/v5-migration-guide#Event-changes-Component-events)
   154	 * @template {Record<string, any>} [EventMap = any]
   155	 * @returns {EventDispatcher<EventMap>}
   156	 */
   157	export function createEventDispatcher() {
   158	        const active_component_context = component_context;
   159	        if (active_component_context === null) {
   160	                e.lifecycle_outside_component('createEventDispatcher');
   161	        }
   162	
   163	        return (type, detail, options) => {
   164	                const events = /** @type {Record<string, Function | Function[]>} */ (
   165	                        active_component_context.s.$$events
   166	                )?.[/** @type {any} */ (type)];
   167	
   168	                if (events) {
   169	                        const callbacks = is_array(events) ? events.slice() : [events];
   170	                        // TODO are there situations where events could be dispatched
   171	                        // in a server (non-DOM) environment?
   172	                        const event = create_custom_event(/** @type {string} */ (type), detail, options);
   173	                        for (const fn of callbacks) {
   174	                                fn.call(active_component_context.x, event);
   175	                        }
   176	                        return !event.defaultPrevented;
   177	                }
   178	
   179	                return true;
   180	        };
   181	}
   182	
   183	// TODO mark beforeUpdate and afterUpdate as deprecated in Svelte 6
   184	
   185	/**
   186	 * Schedules a callback to run immediately before the component is updated after any state change.
   187	 *
   188	 * The first time the callback runs will be before the initial `onMount`.
   189	 *
   190	 * In runes mode use `$effect.pre` instead.
   191	 *
   192	 * @deprecated Use [`$effect.pre`](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/$effect#$effect.pre) instead
   193	 * @param {() => void} fn
   194	 * @returns {void}
   195	 */
   196	export function beforeUpdate(fn) {
   197	        if (component_context === null) {
   198	                e.lifecycle_outside_component('beforeUpdate');
   199	        }
   200	
   201	        if (component_context.l === null) {
   202	                e.lifecycle_legacy_only('beforeUpdate');
   203	        }
   204	
   205	        init_update_callbacks(component_context).b.push(fn);
   206	}
   207	
   208	/**
   209	 * Schedules a callback to run immediately after the component has been updated.
   210	 *
   211	 * The first time the callback runs will be after the initial `onMount`.
   212	 *
   213	 * In runes mode use `$effect` instead.
   214	 *
   215	 * @deprecated Use [`$effect`](https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/$effect) instead
   216	 * @param {() => void} fn
   217	 * @returns {void}
   218	 */
   219	export function afterUpdate(fn) {
   220	        if (component_context === null) {
   221	                e.lifecycle_outside_component('afterUpdate');
   222	        }
   223	
   224	        if (component_context.l === null) {
   225	                e.lifecycle_legacy_only('afterUpdate');
   226	        }
   227	
   228	        init_update_callbacks(component_context).a.push(fn);
   229	}
   230	
   231	/**
   232	 * Legacy-mode: Init callbacks object for onMount/beforeUpdate/afterUpdate
   233	 * @param {ComponentContext} context
   234	 */
   235	function init_update_callbacks(context) {
   236	        var l = /** @type {ComponentContextLegacy} */ (context).l;
   237	        return (l.u ??= { a: [], b: [], m: [] });
   238	}

    63	export class Batch {
    64	        /**

    66	         * They keys of this map are identical to `this.#previous`
    67	         * @type {Map<Source, any>}

    70	
    71	        /**

    73	         * They keys of this map are identical to `this.#current`
    74	         * @type {Map<Source, any>}

    76	        #previous = new Map();
    77

    95	        #deferred = null;

   101	        #neutered = false;
   102

   116	        #boundary_async_effects = [];
   117

   119	         * Template effects and `$effect.pre` effects, which run when

   123	        #render_effects = [];

   129	        #effects = [];

   131	        /**

   136	        #block_effects = [];

   151	
   152	                /** @type {Map<Source, { v: unknown, wv: number }> | null} */
   153	                var current_values = null;
   154	
   155	                // if there are multiple batches, we are 'time travelling' —
   156	                // we need to undo the changes belonging to any batch
   157	                // other than the current one
   158	                if (batches.size > 1) {
   159	                        current_values = new Map();
   160	                        batch_deriveds = new Map();

   163	                                current_values.set(source, { v: source.v, wv: source.wv });
   164	                                source.v = current;
   165	                        }

   168	                                if (batch === this) continue;
   169

   171	                                        if (!current_values.has(source)) {

   173	                                                source.v = previous;
   174	                                        }
   175	                                }
   176	                        }
   177	                }
   178	
   179	                for (const root of root_effects) {
   180	                        this.#traverse_effect_tree(root);
   181	                }
   182	
   183	                // if we didn't start any new async work, and no async work
   184	                // is outstanding from a previous flush, commit
   185	                if (this.#async_effects.length === 0 && this.#pending === 0) {
   186	                        var render_effects = this.#render_effects;
   187	                        var effects = this.#effects;
   188	
   189	                        this.#render_effects = [];
   190	                        this.#effects = [];
   191	                        this.#block_effects = [];
   192

   196	                        flush_queued_effects(effects);
   197	
   198	                        this.#deferred?.resolve();
   199	                } else {
   200	                        // otherwise mark effects clean so they get scheduled on the next run
   201	                        for (const e of this.#render_effects) set_signal_status(e, CLEAN);
   202	                        for (const e of this.#effects) set_signal_status(e, CLEAN);
   203	                        for (const e of this.#block_effects) set_signal_status(e, CLEAN);
   204	                }
   205	
   206	                if (current_values) {
   207	                        for (const [source, { v, wv }] of current_values) {
   208	                                // reset the source to the current value (unless
   209	                                // it got a newer value as a result of effects running)
   210	                                if (source.wv <= wv) {
   211	                                        source.v = v;
   212	                                }
   213	                        }
   214	
   215	                        batch_deriveds = null;
   216	                }
   217	
   218	                for (const effect of this.#async_effects) {
   219	                        update_effect(effect);
   220	                }
   221	
   222	                for (const effect of this.#boundary_async_effects) {
   223	                        update_effect(effect);
   224	                }
   225	
   226	                this.#async_effects = [];
   227	                this.#boundary_async_effects = [];
   228	        }
   229	
   230	        /**
   231	         * Traverse the effect tree, executing effects or stashing
   232	         * them for later execution as appropriate
   233	         * @param {Effect} root
   234	         */
   235	        #traverse_effect_tree(root) {
   236	                root.f ^= CLEAN;
   237	
   238	                var effect = root.first;
   239	
   240	                while (effect !== null) {
   241	                        var flags = effect.f;
   242	                        var is_branch = (flags & (BRANCH_EFFECT | ROOT_EFFECT)) !== 0;
   243	                        var is_skippable_branch = is_branch && (flags & CLEAN) !== 0;
   244	
   245	                        var skip = is_skippable_branch || (flags & INERT) !== 0 || this.skipped_effects.has(effect);
   246	
   247	                        if (!skip && effect.fn !== null) {
   248	                                if (is_branch) {
   249	                                        effect.f ^= CLEAN;
   250	                                } else if ((flags & EFFECT) !== 0) {
   251	                                        this.#effects.push(effect);
   252	                                } else if (async_mode_flag && (flags & RENDER_EFFECT) !== 0) {
   253	                                        this.#render_effects.push(effect);
   254	                                } else if (is_dirty(effect)) {
   255	                                        if ((flags & ASYNC) !== 0) {
   256	                                                var effects = effect.b?.pending ? this.#boundary_async_effects : this.#async_effects;
   257	                                                effects.push(effect);
   258	                                        } else {
   259	                                                if ((effect.f & BLOCK_EFFECT) !== 0) this.#block_effects.push(effect);
   260	                                                update_effect(effect);
   261	                                        }
   262	                                }
   263	
   264	                                var child = effect.first;
   265	
   266	                                if (child !== null) {
   267	                                        effect = child;
   268	                                        continue;
   269	                                }
   270	                        }
   271	
   272	                        var parent = effect.parent;
   273	                        effect = effect.next;
   274	
   275	                        while (effect === null && parent !== null) {
   276	                                effect = parent.next;
   277	                                parent = parent.parent;
   278	                        }
   279	                }
   280	        }
   281	
   282	        /**
   283	         * Associate a change to a given source with the current
   284	         * batch, noting its previous and current values
   285	         * @param {Source} source
   286	         * @param {any} value
   287	         */
   288	        capture(source, value) {
   289	                if (!this.#previous.has(source)) {
   290	                        this.#previous.set(source, value);
   291	                }
   292	
   293	                this.#current.set(source, source.v);
   294	        }
   295	
   296	        activate() {
   297	                current_batch = this;
   298	        }
   299	
   300	        deactivate() {
   301	                current_batch = null;
   302	
   303	                for (const update of effect_pending_updates) {
   304	                        effect_pending_updates.delete(update);
   305	                        update();
   306	
   307	                        if (current_batch !== null) {
   308	                                // only do one at a time
   309	                                break;
   310	                        }
   311	                }
   312	        }
   313	
   314	        neuter() {
   315	                this.#neutered = true;
   316	        }
   317	
   318	        flush() {
   319	                if (queued_root_effects.length > 0) {
   320	                        this.flush_effects();
   321	                } else {
   322	                        this.#commit();
   323	                }
   324	
   325	                if (current_batch !== this) {
   326	                        // this can happen if a `flushSync` occurred during `this.flush_effects()`,
   327	                        // which is permitted in legacy mode despite being a terrible idea
   328	                        return;
   329	                }
   330	
   331	                if (this.#pending === 0) {
   332	                        batches.delete(this);
   333	                }
   334	
   335	                this.deactivate();
   336	        }
   337	
   338	        flush_effects() {
   339	                var was_updating_effect = is_updating_effect;
   340	                is_flushing = true;
   341	
   342	                try {
   343	                        var flush_count = 0;
   344	                        set_is_updating_effect(true);
   345	
   346	                        while (queued_root_effects.length > 0) {
   347	                                if (flush_count++ > 1000) {
   348	                                        infinite_loop_guard();
   349	                                }
   350	
   351	                                this.#process(queued_root_effects);
   352	                                old_values.clear();
   353	                        }
   354	                } finally {
   355	                        is_flushing = false;
   356	                        set_is_updating_effect(was_updating_effect);
   357	
   358	                        last_scheduled_effect = null;
   359	                        if (DEV) {
   360	                                dev_effect_stack = [];
   361	                        }
   362	                }
   363	        }
   364	
   365	        /**
   366	         * Append and remove branches to/from the DOM
   367	         */
   368	        #commit() {
   369	                if (!this.#neutered) {
   370	                        for (const fn of this.#callbacks) {
   371	                                fn();
   372	                        }
   373	                }
   374	
   375	                this.#callbacks.clear();
   376	        }
   377	
   378	        increment() {
   379	                this.#pending += 1;
   380	        }
   381	
   382	        decrement() {
   383	                this.#pending -= 1;
   384	
   385	                if (this.#pending === 0) {
   386	                        for (const e of this.#render_effects) {
   387	                                set_signal_status(e, DIRTY);
   388	                                schedule_effect(e);
   389	                        }
   390	
   391	                        for (const e of this.#effects) {
   392	                                set_signal_status(e, DIRTY);
   393	                                schedule_effect(e);
   394	                        }
   395	
   396	                        for (const e of this.#block_effects) {
   397	                                set_signal_status(e, DIRTY);
   398	                                schedule_effect(e);
   399	                        }
   400	
   401	                        this.#render_effects = [];
   402	                        this.#effects = [];
   403	
   404	                        this.flush();
   405	                } else {
   406	                        this.deactivate();
   407	                }
   408	        }
   409	
   410	        /** @param {() => void} fn */
   411	        add_callback(fn) {
   412	                this.#callbacks.add(fn);
   413	        }
   414	
   415	        settled() {
   416	                return (this.#deferred ??= deferred()).promise;
   417	        }
   418	
   419	        static ensure(autoflush = true) {
   420	                if (current_batch === null) {
   421	                        const batch = (current_batch = new Batch());
   422	                        batches.add(current_batch);
   423	
   424	                        if (autoflush) {
   425	                                queueMicrotask(() => {
   426	                                        if (current_batch !== batch) {
   427	                                                // a flushSync happened in the meantime
   428	                                                return;
   429	                                        }
   430	
   431	                                        batch.flush();
   432	                                });
   433	                        }
   434	                }
   435	
   436	                return current_batch;
   437	        }
   438	}
   439	
   440	/**
   441	 * Synchronously flush any pending updates.
   442	 * Returns void if no callback is provided, otherwise returns the result of calling the callback.
   443	 * @template [T=void]
   444	 * @param {(() => T) | undefined} [fn]
   445	 * @returns {T}
   446	 */
   447	export function flushSync(fn) {
   448	        if (async_mode_flag && active_effect !== null) {
   449	                e.flush_sync_in_effect();
   450	        }
   451	
   452	        var result;
   453	
   454	        const batch = Batch.ensure(false);
   455	
   456	        if (fn) {
   457	                batch.flush_effects();
   458	
   459	                result = fn();
   460	        }
   461	
   462	        while (true) {
   463	                flush_tasks();
   464	
   465	                if (queued_root_effects.length === 0) {
   466	                        if (batch === current_batch) {
   467	                                batch.flush();
   468	                        }
   469	
   470	                        // this would be reset in `batch.flush_effects()` but since we are early returning here,
   471	                        // we need to reset it here as well in case the first time there's 0 queued root effects
   472	                        last_scheduled_effect = null;
   473	
   474	                        if (DEV) {
   475	                                dev_effect_stack = [];
   476	                        }
   477	
   478	                        return /** @type {T} */ (result);
   479	                }
   480	
   481	                batch.flush_effects();
   482	        }
   483	}
   484	
   485	function log_effect_stack() {
   486	        // eslint-disable-next-line no-console
   487	        console.error(
   488	                'Last ten effects were: ',
   489	                dev_effect_stack.slice(-10).map((d) => d.fn)
   490	        );
   491	        dev_effect_stack = [];
   492	}
   493	
   494	function infinite_loop_guard() {
   495	        try {
   496	                e.effect_update_depth_exceeded();
   497	        } catch (error) {
   498	                if (DEV) {
   499	                        // stack is garbage, ignore. Instead add a console.error message.
   500	                        define_property(error, 'stack', {
   501	                                value: ''
   502	                        });
   503	                }
   504	                // Try and handle the error so it can be caught at a boundary, that's
   505	                // if there's an effect available from when it was last scheduled
   506	                if (last_scheduled_effect !== null) {
   507	                        if (DEV) {
   508	                                try {
   509	                                        invoke_error_boundary(error, last_scheduled_effect);
   510	                                } catch (e) {
   511	                                        // Only log the effect stack if the error is re-thrown
   512	                                        log_effect_stack();
   513	                                        throw e;
   514	                                }
   515	                        } else {
   516	                                invoke_error_boundary(error, last_scheduled_effect);
   517	                        }
   518	                } else {
   519	                        if (DEV) {
   520	                                log_effect_stack();
   521	                        }
   522	                        throw error;
   523	                }
   524	        }
   525	}
   526	
   527	/**
   528	 * @param {Array<Effect>} effects
   529	 * @returns {void}
   530	 */
   531	function flush_queued_effects(effects) {
   532	        var length = effects.length;
   533	        if (length === 0) return;
   534	
   535	        for (var i = 0; i < length; i++) {
   536	                var effect = effects[i];
   537	
   538	                if ((effect.f & (DESTROYED | INERT)) === 0) {
   539	                        if (is_dirty(effect)) {
   540	                                var wv = write_version;
   541	
   542	                                update_effect(effect);
   543	
   544	                                // Effects with no dependencies or teardown do not get added to the effect tree.
   545	                                // Deferred effects (e.g. `$effect(...)`) _are_ added to the tree because we
   546	                                // don't know if we need to keep them until they are executed. Doing the check
   547	                                // here (rather than in `update_effect`) allows us to skip the work for
   548	                                // immediate effects.
   549	                                if (effect.deps === null && effect.first === null && effect.nodes_start === null) {
   550	                                        if (effect.teardown === null) {
   551	                                                // remove this effect from the graph
   552	                                                unlink_effect(effect);
   553	                                        } else {
   554	                                                // keep the effect in the graph, but free up some memory
   555	                                                effect.fn = null;
   556	                                        }
   557	                                }
   558	
   559	                                // if state is written in a user effect, abort and re-schedule, lest we run
   560	                                // effects that should be removed as a result of the state change
   561	                                if (write_version > wv && (effect.f & USER_EFFECT) !== 0) {
   562	                                        break;
   563	                                }
   564	                        }
   565	                }
   566	        }
   567	
   568	        for (; i < length; i += 1) {
   569	                schedule_effect(effects[i]);
   570	        }
   571	}
   572	
   573	/**
   574	 * @param {Effect} signal
   575	 * @returns {void}
   576	 */
   577	export function schedule_effect(signal) {
   578	        var effect = (last_scheduled_effect = signal);
   579	
   580	        while (effect.parent !== null) {
   581	                effect = effect.parent;
   582	                var flags = effect.f;
   583	
   584	                // if the effect is being scheduled because a parent (each/await/etc) block
   585	                // updated an internal source, bail out or we'll cause a second flush
   586	                if (is_flushing && effect === active_effect && (flags & BLOCK_EFFECT) !== 0) {
   587	                        return;
   588	                }
   589	
   590	                if ((flags & (ROOT_EFFECT | BRANCH_EFFECT)) !== 0) {
   591	                        if ((flags & CLEAN) === 0) return;
   592	                        effect.f ^= CLEAN;
   593	                }
   594	        }
   595	
   596	        queued_root_effects.push(effect);
   597	}
   598	
   599	export function suspend() {
   600	        var boundary = get_pending_boundary();
   601	        var batch = /** @type {Batch} */ (current_batch);
   602	        var pending = boundary.pending;
   603	
   604	        boundary.update_pending_count(1);
   605	        if (!pending) batch.increment();
   606	
   607	        return function unsuspend() {
   608	                boundary.update_pending_count(-1);
   609	                if (!pending) batch.decrement();
   610	
   611	                unset_context();
   612	        };
   613	}
   614	
   615	/**
   616	 * Forcibly remove all current batches, to prevent cross-talk between tests
   617	 */
   618	export function clear() {
   619	        batches.clear();
   620	}

    67	function push_effect(effect, parent_effect) {
    68	        var parent_last = parent_effect.last;
    69	        if (parent_last === null) {
    70	                parent_effect.last = parent_effect.first = effect;
    71	        } else {
    72	                parent_last.next = effect;
    73	                effect.prev = parent_last;

   214	 * Internal representation of `$effect.pre(...)`
   215	 * @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn
   216	 * @returns {Effect}
   217	 */
   218	export function user_pre_effect(fn) {
   219	        validate_effect('$effect.pre');
   220	        if (DEV) {
   221	                define_property(fn, 'name', {
   222	                        value: '$effect.pre'
   223	                });
   224	        }
   225	        return create_effect(RENDER_EFFECT | USER_EFFECT, fn, true);
   226	}
   227	
   228	/** @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn */
   229	export function inspect_effect(fn) {
   230	        return create_effect(INSPECT_EFFECT, fn, true);
   231	}
   232	
   233	/**
   234	 * Internal representation of `$effect.root(...)`
   235	 * @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn
   236	 * @returns {() => void}
   237	 */
   238	export function effect_root(fn) {
   239	        Batch.ensure();
   240	        const effect = create_effect(ROOT_EFFECT, fn, true);
   241	
   242	        return () => {
   243	                destroy_effect(effect);
   244	        };
   245	}
   246	
   247	/**
   248	 * An effect root whose children can transition out
   249	 * @param {() => void} fn
   250	 * @returns {(options?: { outro?: boolean }) => Promise<void>}
   251	 */
   252	export function component_root(fn) {
   253	        Batch.ensure();
   254	        const effect = create_effect(ROOT_EFFECT, fn, true);
   255	
   256	        return (options = {}) => {
   257	                return new Promise((fulfil) => {
   258	                        if (options.outro) {
   259	                                pause_effect(effect, () => {
   260	                                        destroy_effect(effect);
   261	                                        fulfil(undefined);
   262	                                });
   263	                        } else {
   264	                                destroy_effect(effect);
   265	                                fulfil(undefined);
   266	                        }
   267	                });
   268	        };
   269	}
   270	
   271	/**
   272	 * @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn
   273	 * @returns {Effect}
   274	 */
   275	export function effect(fn) {
   276	        return create_effect(EFFECT, fn, false);
   277	}
   278	
   279	/**
   280	 * Internal representation of `$: ..`
   281	 * @param {() => any} deps
   282	 * @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn
   283	 */
   284	export function legacy_pre_effect(deps, fn) {
   285	        var context = /** @type {ComponentContextLegacy} */ (component_context);
   286	
   287	        /** @type {{ effect: null | Effect, ran: boolean, deps: () => any }} */
   288	        var token = { effect: null, ran: false, deps };
   289	
   290	        context.l.$.push(token);
   291	
   292	        token.effect = render_effect(() => {
   293	                deps();
   294	
   295	                // If this legacy pre effect has already run before the end of the reset, then
   296	                // bail out to emulate the same behavior.
   297	                if (token.ran) return;
   298	
   299	                token.ran = true;
   300	                untrack(fn);

   178	/**
   179	 * Internal representation of `$effect(...)`
   180	 * @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn
   181	 */
   182	export function user_effect(fn) {
   183	        validate_effect('$effect');
   184	
   185	        if (DEV) {
   186	                define_property(fn, 'name', {
   187	                        value: '$effect'
   188	                });
   189	        }
   190	
   191	        // Non-nested `$effect(...)` in a component should be deferred
   192	        // until the component is mounted
   193	        var flags = /** @type {Effect} */ (active_effect).f;
   194	        var defer = !active_reaction && (flags & BRANCH_EFFECT) !== 0 && (flags & EFFECT_RAN) === 0;
   195	
   196	        if (defer) {
   197	                // Top-level `$effect(...)` in an unmounted component — defer until mount
   198	                var context = /** @type {ComponentContext} */ (component_context);
   199	                (context.e ??= []).push(fn);
   200	        } else {
   201	                // Everything else — create immediately
   202	                return create_user_effect(fn);
   203	        }
   204	}
   205	
   206	/**
   207	 * @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn
   208	 */
   209	export function create_user_effect(fn) {
   210	        return create_effect(EFFECT | USER_EFFECT, fn, false);

    79	 * @param {number} type
    80	 * @param {null | (() => void | (() => void))} fn
    81	 * @param {boolean} sync
    82	 * @param {boolean} push
    83	 * @returns {Effect}
    84	 */
    85	function create_effect(type, fn, sync, push = true) {
    86	        var parent = active_effect;
    87	
    88	        if (DEV) {
    89	                // Ensure the parent is never an inspect effect
    90	                while (parent !== null && (parent.f & INSPECT_EFFECT) !== 0) {
    91	                        parent = parent.parent;
    92	                }
    93	        }
    94	
    95	        if (parent !== null && (parent.f & INERT) !== 0) {
    96	                type |= INERT;
    97	        }
    98	
    99	        /** @type {Effect} */
   100	        var effect = {
   101	                ctx: component_context,
   102	                deps: null,
   103	                nodes_start: null,
   104	                nodes_end: null,
   105	                f: type | DIRTY,
   106	                first: null,
   107	                fn,
   108	                last: null,
   109	                next: null,
   110	                parent,
   111	                b: parent && parent.b,
   112	                prev: null,
   113	                teardown: null,
   114	                transitions: null,
   115	                wv: 0,
   116	                ac: null
   117	        };
   118

   120	                effect.component_function = dev_current_component_function;
   121	        }
   122	
   123	        if (sync) {
   124	                try {
   125	                        update_effect(effect);
   126	                        effect.f |= EFFECT_RAN;
   127	                } catch (e) {
   128	                        destroy_effect(effect);
   129	                        throw e;
   130	                }
   131	        } else if (fn !== null) {
   132	                schedule_effect(effect);
   133	        }
   134	
   135	        // if an effect has no dependencies, no DOM and no teardown function,
   136	        // don't bother adding it to the effect tree
   137	        var inert =
   138	                sync &&
   139	                effect.deps === null &&
   140	                effect.first === null &&
   141	                effect.nodes_start === null &&
   142	                effect.teardown === null &&

   144

   146	                if (parent !== null) {
   147	                        push_effect(effect, parent);
   148	                }

   151	                if (active_reaction !== null && (active_reaction.f & DERIVED) !== 0) {
   152	                        var derived = /** @type {Derived} */ (active_reaction);
   153	                        (derived.effects ??= []).push(effect);
   154	                }
   155	        }
   156	
   157	        return effect;
   158	}

   527	/**
   528	 * @param {Array<Effect>} effects
   529	 * @returns {void}
   530	 */
   531	function flush_queued_effects(effects) {
   532	        var length = effects.length;
   533	        if (length === 0) return;
   534	
   535	        for (var i = 0; i < length; i++) {
   536	                var effect = effects[i];
   537	
   538	                if ((effect.f & (DESTROYED | INERT)) === 0) {
   539	                        if (is_dirty(effect)) {
   540	                                var wv = write_version;
   541	
   542	                                update_effect(effect);
   543	
   544	                                // Effects with no dependencies or teardown do not get added to the effect tree.
   545	                                // Deferred effects (e.g. `$effect(...)`) _are_ added to the tree because we
   546	                                // don't know if we need to keep them until they are executed. Doing the check
   547	                                // here (rather than in `update_effect`) allows us to skip the work for
   548	                                // immediate effects.
   549	                                if (effect.deps === null && effect.first === null && effect.nodes_start === null) {
   550	                                        if (effect.teardown === null) {
   551	                                                // remove this effect from the graph
   552	                                                unlink_effect(effect);
   553	                                        } else {
   554	                                                // keep the effect in the graph, but free up some memory
   555	                                                effect.fn = null;
   556	                                        }
   557	                                }
   558	
   559	                                // if state is written in a user effect, abort and re-schedule, lest we run
   560	                                // effects that should be removed as a result of the state change
   561	                                if (write_version > wv && (effect.f & USER_EFFECT) !== 0) {
   562	                                        break;
   563	                                }
   564	                        }
   565	                }
   566	        }
   567	
   568	        for (; i < length; i += 1) {
   569	                schedule_effect(effects[i]);
   570	        }
   571	}

   540	export function get(signal) {
   541	        var flags = signal.f;
   542	        var is_derived = (flags & DERIVED) !== 0;
   543	
   544	        if (captured_signals !== null) {
   545	                captured_signals.add(signal);
   546	        }
   547	
   548	        // Register the dependency on the current reaction signal.
   549	        if (active_reaction !== null && !untracking) {
   550	                // if we're in a derived that is being read inside an _async_ derived,
   551	                // it's possible that the effect was already destroyed. In this case,
   552	                // we don't add the dependency, because that would create a memory leak
   553	                var destroyed = active_effect !== null && (active_effect.f & DESTROYED) !== 0;
   554	
   555	                if (!destroyed && !current_sources?.includes(signal)) {
   556	                        var deps = active_reaction.deps;
   557	
   558	                        if ((active_reaction.f & REACTION_IS_UPDATING) !== 0) {
   559	                                // we're in the effect init/update cycle
   560	                                if (signal.rv < read_version) {
   561	                                        signal.rv = read_version;
   562	
   563	                                        // If the signal is accessing the same dependencies in the same
   564	                                        // order as it did last time, increment `skipped_deps`
   565	                                        // rather than updating `new_deps`, which creates GC cost
   566	                                        if (new_deps === null && deps !== null && deps[skipped_deps] === signal) {
   567	                                                skipped_deps++;
   568	                                        } else if (new_deps === null) {
   569	                                                new_deps = [signal];
   570	                                        } else if (!skip_reaction || !new_deps.includes(signal)) {
   571	                                                // Normally we can push duplicated dependencies to `new_deps`, but if we're inside
   572	                                                // an unowned derived because skip_reaction is true, then we need to ensure that
   573	                                                // we don't have duplicates
   574	                                                new_deps.push(signal);
   575	                                        }
   576	                                }
   577	                        } else {
   578	                                // we're adding a dependency outside the init/update cycle
   579	                                // (i.e. after an `await`)
   580	                                (active_reaction.deps ??= []).push(signal);
   581

    79	                signal.set_during_effect = false;
    80	                signal.trace = null;
    81	        }
    82

    84	}

     1	---
     2	title: Testing
     3	---
     4	
     5	Testing helps you write and maintain your code and guard against regressions. Testing frameworks help you with that, allowing you to describe assertions or expectations about how your code should behave. Svelte is unopinionated about which testing framework you use — you can write unit tests, integration tests, and end-to-end tests using solutions like [Vitest](https://vitest.dev/), [Jasmine](https://jasmine.github.io/), [Cypress](https://www.cypress.io/) and [Playwright](https://playwright.dev/).
     6	
     7	## Unit and integration testing using Vitest
     8	
     9	Unit tests allow you to test small isolated parts of your code. Integration tests allow you to test parts of your application to see if they work together. If you're using Vite (including via SvelteKit), we recommend using [Vitest](https://vitest.dev/). You can use the Svelte CLI to [setup Vitest](/docs/cli/vitest) either during project creation or later on.
    10	
    11	To setup Vitest manually, first install it:
    12	
    13	```bash
    14	npm install -D vitest
    15	```
    16	
    17	Then adjust your `vite.config.js`:
    18	
    19	<!-- prettier-ignore -->
    20	```js
    21	/// file: vite.config.js
    22	import { defineConfig } from +++'vitest/config'+++;
    23	
    24	export default defineConfig({
    25	        // ...
    26	        // Tell Vitest to use the `browser` entry points in `package.json` files, even though it's running in Node
    27	        resolve: process.env.VITEST
    28	                ? {
    29	                                conditions: ['browser']
    30	                        }
    31	                : undefined
    32	});
    33	```
    34	
    35	> [!NOTE] If loading the browser version of all your packages is undesirable, because (for example) you also test backend libraries, [you may need to resort to an alias configuration](https://github.com/testing-library/svelte-testing-library/issues/222#issuecomment-1909993331)
    36	
    37	You can now write unit tests for code inside your `.js/.ts` files:
    38	
    39	```js
    40	/// file: multiplier.svelte.test.js
    41	import { flushSync } from 'svelte';
    42	import { expect, test } from 'vitest';
    43	import { multiplier } from './multiplier.svelte.js';
    44	
    45	test('Multiplier', () => {
    46	        let double = multiplier(0, 2);
    47	
    48	        expect(double.value).toEqual(0);
    49	
    50	        double.set(5);
    51	
    52	        expect(double.value).toEqual(10);
    53	});
    54	```
    55	
    56	```js
    57	/// file: multiplier.svelte.js
    58	/**
    59	 * @param {number} initial
    60	 * @param {number} k
    61	 */
    62	export function multiplier(initial, k) {
    63	        let count = $state(initial);
    64	
    65	        return {
    66	                get value() {
    67	                        return count * k;
    68	                },
    69	                /** @param {number} c */
    70	                set: (c) => {
    71	                        count = c;
    72	                }
    73	        };
    74	}
    75	```
    76	
    77	### Using runes inside your test files
    78	
    79	Since Vitest processes your test files the same way as your source files, you can use runes inside your tests as long as the filename includes `.svelte`:
    80	
    81	```js
    82	/// file: multiplier.svelte.test.js
    83	import { flushSync } from 'svelte';
    84	import { expect, test } from 'vitest';
    85	import { multiplier } from './multiplier.svelte.js';
    86	
    87	test('Multiplier', () => {
    88	        let count = $state(0);
    89	        let double = multiplier(() => count, 2);
    90	
    91	        expect(double.value).toEqual(0);
    92	
    93	        count = 5;
    94	
    95	        expect(double.value).toEqual(10);
    96	});
    97	```
    98	
    99	```js
   100	/// file: multiplier.svelte.js
   101	/**
   102	 * @param {() => number} getCount
   103	 * @param {number} k
   104	 */
   105	export function multiplier(getCount, k) {
   106	        return {
   107	                get value() {
   108	                        return getCount() * k;
   109	                }
   110	        };
   111	}
   112	```
   113	
   114	If the code being tested uses effects, you need to wrap the test inside `$effect.root`:
   115	
   116	```js
   117	/// file: logger.svelte.test.js
   118	import { flushSync } from 'svelte';
   119	import { expect, test } from 'vitest';
   120	import { logger } from './logger.svelte.js';
   121	
   122	test('Effect', () => {
   123	        const cleanup = $effect.root(() => {
   124	                let count = $state(0);
   125	
   126	                // logger uses an $effect to log updates of its input
   127	                let log = logger(() => count);
   128	
   129	                // effects normally run after a microtask,
   130	                // use flushSync to execute all pending effects synchronously
   131	                flushSync();
   132	                expect(log).toEqual([0]);
   133	
   134	                count = 1;
   135	                flushSync();
   136	
   137	                expect(log).toEqual([0, 1]);
   138	        });
   139	
   140	        cleanup();
   141	});
   142	```
   143	
   144	```js
   145	/// file: logger.svelte.js
   146	/**
   147	 * @param {() => any} getValue
   148	 */
   149	export function logger(getValue) {
   150	        /** @type {any[]} */
   151	        let log = [];
   152	
   153	        $effect(() => {
   154	                log.push(getValue());
   155	        });
   156	
   157	        return log;
   158	}
   159	```
   160	
   161	### Component testing
   162	
   163	It is possible to test your components in isolation using Vitest.
   164	
   165	> [!NOTE] Before writing component tests, think about whether you actually need to test the component, or if it's more about the logic _inside_ the component. If so, consider extracting out that logic to test it in isolation, without the overhead of a component
   166	
   167	To get started, install jsdom (a library that shims DOM APIs):
   168	
   169	```bash
   170	npm install -D jsdom
   171	```
   172	
   173	Then adjust your `vite.config.js`:
   174	
   175	```js
   176	/// file: vite.config.js
   177	import { defineConfig } from 'vitest/config';
   178	
   179	export default defineConfig({
   180	        plugins: [
   181	                /* ... */
   182	        ],
   183	        test: {
   184	                // If you are testing components client-side, you need to setup a DOM environment.
   185	                // If not all your files should have this environment, you can use a
   186	                // `// @vitest-environment jsdom` comment at the top of the test files instead.
   187	                environment: 'jsdom'
   188	        },
   189	        // Tell Vitest to use the `browser` entry points in `package.json` files, even though it's running in Node
   190	        resolve: process.env.VITEST
   191	                ? {
   192	                                conditions: ['browser']
   193	                        }
   194	                : undefined
   195	});
   196	```
   197	
   198	After that, you can create a test file in which you import the component to test, interact with it programmatically and write expectations about the results:
   199	
   200	```js
   201	/// file: component.test.js
   202	import { flushSync, mount, unmount } from 'svelte';
   203	import { expect, test } from 'vitest';
   204	import Component from './Component.svelte';
   205	
   206	test('Component', () => {
   207	        // Instantiate the component using Svelte's `mount` API
   208	        const component = mount(Component, {
   209	                target: document.body, // `document` exists because of jsdom
   210	                props: { initial: 0 }
   211	        });
   212	
   213	        expect(document.body.innerHTML).toBe('<button>0</button>');
   214	
   215	        // Click the button, then flush the changes so you can synchronously write expectations
   216	        document.body.querySelector('button').click();
   217	        flushSync();
   218	
   219	        expect(document.body.innerHTML).toBe('<button>1</button>');
   220	
   221	        // Remove the component from the DOM
   222	        unmount(component);
   223	});
   224	```
   225	
   226	While the process is very straightforward, it is also low level and somewhat brittle, as the precise structure of your component may change frequently. Tools like [@testing-library/svelte](https://testing-library.com/docs/svelte-testing-library/intro/) can help streamline your tests. The above test could be rewritten like this:
   227	
   228	```js
   229	/// file: component.test.js
   230	import { render, screen } from '@testing-library/svelte';
   231	import userEvent from '@testing-library/user-event';
   232	import { expect, test } from 'vitest';
   233	import Component from './Component.svelte';
   234	
   235	test('Component', async () => {
   236	        const user = userEvent.setup();
   237	        render(Component);
   238	
   239	        const button = screen.getByRole('button');
   240	        expect(button).toHaveTextContent(0);
   241	
   242	        await user.click(button);
   243	        expect(button).toHaveTextContent(1);
   244	});
   245	```
   246	
   247	When writing component tests that involve two-way bindings, context or snippet props, it's best to create a wrapper component for your specific test and interact with that. `@testing-library/svelte` contains some [examples](https://testing-library.com/docs/svelte-testing-library/example).
   248	
   249	## E2E tests using Playwright
   250	
   251	E2E (short for 'end to end') tests allow you to test your full application through the eyes of the user. This section uses [Playwright](https://playwright.dev/) as an example, but you can also use other solutions like [Cypress](https://www.cypress.io/) or [NightwatchJS](https://nightwatchjs.org/).
   252	
   253	You can use the Svelte CLI to [setup Playwright](/docs/cli/playwright) either during project creation or later on. You can also [set it up with `npm init playwright`](https://playwright.dev/docs/intro). Additionally, you may also want to install an IDE plugin such as [the VS Code extension](https://playwright.dev/docs/getting-started-vscode) to be able to execute tests from inside your IDE.
   254	
   255	If you've run `npm init playwright` or are not using Vite, you may need to adjust the Playwright config to tell Playwright what to do before running the tests - mainly starting your application at a certain port. For example:
   256	
   257	```js
   258	/// file: playwright.config.js
   259	const config = {
   260	        webServer: {
   261	                command: 'npm run build && npm run preview',
   262	                port: 4173
   263	        },
   264	        testDir: 'tests',
   265	        testMatch: /(.+\.)?(test|spec)\.[jt]s/
   266	};
   267	
   268	export default config;
   269	```
   270	
   271	You can now start writing tests. These are totally unaware of Svelte as a framework, so you mainly interact with the DOM and write assertions.
   272	
   273	```js
   274	// @errors: 2307 7031
   275	/// file: tests/hello-world.spec.js
   276	import { expect, test } from '@playwright/test';
   277	
   278	test('home page has expected h1', async ({ page }) => {
   279	        await page.goto('/');
   280	        await expect(page.locator('h1')).toBeVisible();
   281	});
   282	```
   283

2025-12-26 22:48:39,353 - INFO - swea-agent-sveltejs__svelte-16405 - 💭 THOUGHT
Perfect! I found the documentation. Line 79 says: "Since Vitest processes your test files the same way as your source files, you can use runes inside your tests as long as the filename includes `.svelte`".

So the key is that the test file needs to have `.svelte` in the filename (like `multiplier.svelte.test.js` or `logger.svelte.test.js`). This allows Vitest (with the right plugins) to process the file through the Svelte compiler, which will transform the runes into the actual implementation.

Now, the PR description mentions that this was working in Svelte 5.1.11 but broke in later versions. The issue is likely in the batching/effect scheduling logic. Let me look at the `user_effect` function again more carefully:

Looking back at lines 182-204 in effects.js, I see that `user_effect` has special deferral logic (lines 191-200):

```javascript
var flags = /** @type {Effect} */ (active_effect).f;
var defer = !active_reaction && (flags & BRANCH_EFFECT) !== 0 && (flags & EFFECT_RAN) === 0;

if (defer) {
    // Top-level `$effect(...)` in an unmounted component — defer until mount
    var context = /** @type {ComponentContext} */ (component_context);
    (context.e ??= []).push(fn);
} else {
    // Everything else — create immediately
    return create_user_effect(fn);
}
```

The problem is:
1. When `user_effect` is called inside an `effect_root`, the `active_effect` is the root effect
2. ROOT_EFFECT has flags that include `ROOT_EFFECT` (1 << 6) but not `BRANCH_EFFECT` (1 << 5)
3. So the `defer` condition evaluates to: `!active_reaction && (ROOT_EFFECT & BRANCH_EFFECT) !== 0 && ...`
4. Since `(ROOT_EFFECT & BRANCH_EFFECT) === 0`, the defer condition is false
5. So it creates the effect immediately with `create_user_effect(fn)`

Now let me look more closely at what happens when `user_effect` is scheduled and then executed. The effect gets the `EFFECT | USER_EFFECT` flags. Let me check the processing logic in batch.js again:

At line 250 in batch.js:
```javascript
} else if ((flags & EFFECT) !== 0) {
    this.#effects.push(effect);
```

So USER_EFFECT (which includes EFFECT) gets pushed to `this.#effects` array. Then at line 196:
```javascript
flush_queued_effects(effects);
```

And in `flush_queued_effects` at line 531:
```javascript
for (var i = 0; i < length; i++) {
    var effect = effects[i];

    if ((effect.f & (DESTROYED | INERT)) === 0) {
        if (is_dirty(effect)) {
            var wv = write_version;

            update_effect(effect);

            // Effects with no dependencies or teardown do not get added to the effect tree.
            // Deferred effects (e.g. `$effect(...)`) _are_ added to the tree because we
            // don't know if we need to keep them until they are executed. Doing the check
            // here (rather than in `update_effect`) allows us to skip the work for
            // immediate effects.
            if (effect.deps === null && effect.first === null && effect.nodes_start === null) {
                if (effect.teardown === null) {
                    // remove this effect from the graph
                    unlink_effect(effect);
                } else {
                    // keep the effect in the graph, but free up some memory
                    effect.fn = null;
                }
            }
```

Ah! I see it now. At lines 549-556, if an effect has no dependencies, no children, and no nodes, but has a teardown, it sets `effect.fn = null`. But the condition here assumes that if the effect has teardown, we want to keep it in the graph but don't need the function anymore.

However, the problem is that if an effect's function is set to null, it won't be traversed again in the next batch! Look at line 247 in the `#traverse_effect_tree` method:

```javascript
if (!skip && effect.fn !== null) {
```

This is the bug! Once `effect.fn` is set to null, the effect will never be processed again, even if its dependencies change.

But wait, let me verify this theory more carefully. Let me add more debug output to trace what's happening with the effect.fn:

```javascript
// Effects with no dependencies or teardown do not get added to the effect tree.
// Deferred effects (e.g. `$effect(...)`) _are_ added to the tree because we
// don't know if we need to keep them until they are executed. Doing the check
// here (rather than in `update_effect`) allows us to skip the work for
```

2025-12-26 22:51:48,076 - INFO - swea-agent-sveltejs__svelte-16405 - 💭 THOUGHT
Let me think about this differently. According to the issue, the problem happens when:
1. Using runes (`$state`, `$effect`) in test files
2. The test file has `.svelte` in its name
3. This worked in Svelte 5.1.11 but broke in later versions

The key insight from the documentation is that files with `.svelte` in the name get processed by the Svelte compiler, which transforms runes into actual code. So let me think about what the actual transformed code would look like.

When you write:
```javascript
let count = $state(0);
```

The Svelte compiler transforms it to something like:
```javascript
let count = state(0);
```

Where `state` is imported from the Svelte internal APIs.

And when you write:
```javascript
$effect(() => {
    log.push(count);
});
```

It gets transformed to:
```javascript
user_effect(() => {
    log.push(get(count));
});
```

So the actual issue might be in the transformation or in how the transformed code works. But wait, the PR says it worked in 5.1.11, so something must have changed.

Let me check the release notes or changelog around version 5.1.11:

Now, let me think about the real issue. The PR description says "flushSync() seems to be ignored and code in $effect rune is not run" with the newest versions. But my test shows it does work when using the internal APIs directly.

Wait! I think I understand now. The issue might be that in test files, when you use runes, they need to be inside an `effect_root`. But the documentation example shows creating an effect root and then using `flushSync()` inside it. Let me re-read the doc example:

```javascript
test('Effect', () => {
    const cleanup = $effect.root(() => {
        let count = $state(0);

        // logger uses an $effect to log updates of its input
        let log = logger(() => count);

        // effects normally run after a microtask,
        // use flushSync to execute all pending effects synchronously
        flushSync();
        expect(log).toEqual([0]);

        count = 1;
        flushSync();

        expect(log).toEqual([0, 1]);
    });

    cleanup();
});
```

So the effect_root is created synchronously, which means the effect inside `logger` should be created and scheduled. Then `flushSync()` is called to flush the effects.

The issue might be related to how `effect_root` creates the root and schedules effects. Let me look at that function again:

OK, so `Batch.ensure()` creates a batch if one doesn't exist, and by default schedules it to flush via a microtask. But with `flushSync()`, we flush synchronously.

Now I think the real issue might be different. Let me think about what happens when you call `effect_root()` and then `flushSync()` multiple times:

1. `effect_root(fn)` creates a root effect and runs `fn` synchronously
2. Inside `fn`, we create state and call `user_effect()` 
3. `user_effect()` creates an effect and schedules it
4. First `flushSync()` runs and executes the scheduled effect
5. We update the state
6. Second `flushSync()` should run the effect again

But the issue is: what if the effect doesn't get scheduled properly after the state update? Let me check how state updates schedule effects:

   292	function mark_reactions(signal, status) {
   293	        var reactions = signal.reactions;
   294	        if (reactions === null) return;
   295	
   296	        var runes = is_runes();
   297	        var length = reactions.length;
   298	
   299	        for (var i = 0; i < length; i++) {
   300	                var reaction = reactions[i];
   301	                var flags = reaction.f;
   302	
   303	                // Skip any effects that are already dirty
   304	                if ((flags & DIRTY) !== 0) continue;
   305	
   306	                // In legacy mode, skip the current effect to prevent infinite loops
   307	                if (!runes && reaction === active_effect) continue;
   308	
   309	                // Inspect effects need to run immediately, so that the stack trace makes sense
   310	                if (DEV && (flags & INSPECT_EFFECT) !== 0) {
   311	                        inspect_effects.add(reaction);
   312	                        continue;
   313	                }
   314	
   315	                set_signal_status(reaction, status);
   316	
   317	                // If the signal a) was previously clean or b) is an unowned derived, then mark it
   318	                if ((flags & (CLEAN | UNOWNED)) !== 0) {
   319	                        if ((flags & DERIVED) !== 0) {
   320	                                mark_reactions(/** @type {Derived} */ (reaction), MAYBE_DIRTY);
   321	                        } else {
   322	                                schedule_effect(/** @type {Effect} */ (reaction));
   323	                        }
   324	                }
   325	        }
   326	}
   327

commit 53bbe3462b3c50393eb916c23436bc497dfd82b9
Author: Simon H <5968653+dummdidumm@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Mon Nov 24 16:28:21 2025 +0100

    fix: don't execute attachments and attribute effects eagerly (#17208)
    
    * fix: don't execute attachments and attribute effects eagerly
    
    attributes_effect and attachments are blocks since they need the managed "don't just destroy children effects"-behavior, but they're not block effects in the sense of "run them eagerly while traversing the effect tree or while flushing effects". Since the latter was the case until now, it meant that forks could cause visible UI updates.
    
    This PR introduces a new flag to fix that. `BLOCK_NON_EAGER` is basically a combination of block effects (with respects to the managed behavior) and render effects (with respects to the execution timing).
    
    Fixes https://github.com/sveltejs/kit/issues/14931
    
    * managed_effect

    attributes_effect and attachments are blocks since they need the managed "don't just destroy children effects"-behavior, but they're not block effects in the sense of "run them eagerly while traversing the effect tree or while flushing effects". Since the latter was the case until now, it meant that forks could cause visible UI updates.
    
    This PR introduces a new flag to fix that. `BLOCK_NON_EAGER` is basically a combination of block effects (with respects to the managed behavior) and render effects (with respects to the execution timing).
    
    Fixes https://github.com/sveltejs/kit/issues/14931
    
    * managed_effect

2025-12-26 22:58:00,217 - INFO - swea-agent-sveltejs__svelte-16405 - 💭 THOUGHT
Excellent! It still works. But wait, this fix might not be addressing the actual issue from the PR. Let me think about this more carefully.

The issue described in the PR is:
1. With Svelte > 5.1.11 and vitest 3.2.x: effects don't run (flushSync ignored)
2. With Svelte > 5.1.11 and vitest 3.1.4: effect_update_depth_exceeded error
3. With Svelte 5.1.11 and vitest 3.1.4: works fine

This suggests the issue is not about test isolation per se, but about how effects are scheduled and executed. The `clear()` fix might help with test isolation, but it might not be the root cause.

Let me think about what could cause effects not to run even after `flushSync()`. Looking back at the commit history, I saw a commit about "correctly reschedule deferred effects when reviving a batch after async work". But there might be another issue.

Let me check if there's an issue with how `last_scheduled_effect` is handled. Looking at line 358 and 472 in batch.js, `last_scheduled_effect` is set to null after processing. But what if there's an issue where effects aren't being properly marked as dirty or scheduled?

Actually, looking more carefully at the `clear()` function comment: "Forcibly remove all current batches, to prevent cross-talk between tests". This suggests it's meant to be called between tests. But if current_batch isn't reset, then subsequent tests might reuse a stale batch!

Let me write a test that specifically checks the scenario from the PR description. But first, let me check what happens if we call `clear()` and then try to use effects:

🎬 ACTION
cat > /testbed/test_clear.js << 'EOF'
import { effect_root, user_effect } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js';
import { flushSync } from './packages/svelte/src/index-client.js';
import { source, set } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/sources.js';
import { get } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/runtime.js';
import { clear } from './packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/batch.js';

// Test 1
console.log('=== Test 1 ===');
const log1 = { value: [] };
const cleanup1 = effect_root(() => {
    const count = source(0);

    user_effect(() => {
        log.value.push(get(count));
    });

    flushSync();
    console.log('Test 1 - After first flushSync:', log1.value);

    set(count, 1);
    flushSync();
    console.log('Test 1 - After second flushSync:', log1.value);
});
cleanup1();

// Clear state between tests
console.log('\n=== Clearing state ===\n');
clear();

// Test 2
console.log('=== Test 2 ===');
const log2 = { value: [] };
const cleanup2 = effect_root(() => {
    const count = source(10);

    user_effect(() => {
        log2.value.push(get(count));
    });

    flushSync();
    console.log('Test 2 - After first flushSync:', log2.value);

    set(count, 11);
    flushSync();
    console.log('Test 2 - After second flushSync:', log2.value);
});
cleanup2();

console.log('\n=== All tests completed ===');
